"Silent Hill 2" is a survival horror video game developed by Konami and released in 2001. It's renowned for its psychological horror elements, intricate storytelling, and eerie atmosphere. The game follows James Sunderland as he searches for his deceased wife in the mysterious town of Silent Hill, encountering disturbing creatures and confronting his own inner demons along the way. It's considered a classic in the horror genre and has had a significant impact on gaming culture.

Not sure Iâ€™m entirely convinced that the new fog effects are an improvement. Iâ€™ve been in really thick sea fog and mountain fog. To my mind fog seems eerie because (like the original graphics) it literally is featureless and turns the world into unnaturally smooth layers, the world simply fades into whiteness.  Thereâ€™s a strange sense of both claustrophobia (because it limits you to a visible bubble only a few feet wide) and a feeling of being lost in an immense expanses of nothingness. These new effects make it look like 3D billowing smoke. Which is cool in its own way, but a very different aesthetic.

Beautiful graphics, obviously, but I worry that it removes some of the deliberate ambiguity and therefore the mood. In the original bathroom scene, James's expression is unreadable and his face is cast in deep shadow. He's looking into his eyes, but his eyes are just shadows staring back at him. I think that's an important detail that this remaster is sacrificing in exchange for higher graphical fidelity. But putting that aside, I really hope this remake will recapture the unique tone of the classic game.

When you feel lonely as this character you oddly feel like you're not real but exist in a different world spending years of your life trying to feel real, find meaning to life, find the woman of your dreams but you build barriers and obstacles in your mind to prevent you from getting that such as the monsters that represent them in this game. You are also dealing with an issue that most of the population ain't dealing with so you feel like you're the last person on earth and you just suffer in silence

All these people complaining about the missing "subtle" expressions of the original game... Shut the f*ck up. Ito and the Blooper Team are working hard to make this game. You can clearly see it's not going to be a lazy remake, but a full-of-passion project with a slightly different tone. As the SH2 original creators said, you people are thinking way too much into this.
Now watched it a few times and Bloober has turned James into a typical gruff protag when the entire point of James was to be a completely unspecial guy who has been shut off from his emotions (and indeed his recollection of events). The almost disconnected acting in the original wasn't just to aim for something Lynchian, it was to show how cut off James is, from others but especially from himself. I'm getting none of that from this trailer. Indeed, rather than show how special and unique SH2 is, this just plays out like any generic horror film trailer.  I dunno how Bloober keeps getting projects because their handling of horror is dreadful (especially when it comes to mental health).

The only thing I'm not crazy about here is that James is only sad. James at the start of the original wasn't sad, but depressed, which is a very different thing. He looked cold and distant, and his voice was largely emotionless save for an anger and bitterness that he was barely holding back. There was even a bit of childishness here and there, as though James went through the game largely in a daze. The original performance was ridiculously nuanced and added a lot of impact to every word, and so far I'm not really hearing that latent anger or exhaustion here. Not much trauma in other words. That being said, this new peformance is still miles above Troy Baker's melodramatic take.

With the amount of video essays coming out talking about this title year after year on YT it's only natural for them to make a remake. The question is can the guys from Krakow, Poland make it justice? There's something about the original Japanese SH team that is very special in delivering the atmosphere in their titles. It's this uncanniness that western devs can't seem to grasp based on the previous titles developed in the west. I very much hope it's different in this case but I temper my expectations nonetheless. It's this cleanness, emphasis on the iconic visuals that make me have my doubts. I have a feeling that it's the SH2 people know from the internet instead the one they have played themselves in the past. Despite that wishing the best and kudos to the team for making their dream game :>

Even though its not in the best of hands with bloober, I believe they can make it work. However, the trailer really fails to impress me. Silent Hill has always been ahead of the curve, especially when it comes to graphics. We haven't seen much of the gameplay/in-engine lighting as of yet so it's difficult to speak on that, but the art style concerns me. It's painfully mediocre, to the point where it looks almost *cartoonish,* which is decidedly wrong for the tone of silent hill. Who knows, this may be an incredibly primitive model of the game that will be vastly improved upon, but if bloober's other ventures are anything to go by, we may end up with a game sporting sub-par graphics. Everyone's talking about Akira Yamaoka coming back, but he's done the soundtrack for all Silent Hill games: even the cash grabs made by western developers after Team Silent was disbanded so it's not really surprising. What I'm really excited about is Masahiro Ito: he did the monster designs for the original games and really helped give Silent Hill its ambience. Because he's so passionate about the original designs, he disliked what Konami has done since as they've often reused Pyramid Head for his popularity (ignoring that it's a part of James).  So for Ito to be back, Konami has really started afresh. It looks promising, and I can't wait to see what Bloober does with it.

Cool that this is back, but... why is James so emotional? A huge part of James's character, what makes him so memorable, is that he's so weirdly distant and disconnected from everything. Even his reason for coming to Silent Hill, looking for Mary, he's not totally sure if he should be doing it or if he even wants to. In this, he seems desperate, frustrated, scared, all things that he was in the original, but never showed at all. All of that was reflected in the monsters he fought; they were his pent-up emotions given flesh, while he acted so bizarrely inhuman towards everything going on around him. This new James just feels too dramatic for the sake of being dramatic, for being a relatable protagonist, which James absolutely never was. By making him wear his emotions on his sleeve like this, rather than showcasing how he's felt for years through the monsters he fights, it just makes them weird demons that are in Silent Hill; they're no longer representations of James's feelings about his situation that he's kept repressed all this time, they're just mindless things that want to hurt James, like any other video game enemy.
